<div id="review_1378950554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1378950554" />
    <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction"><img alt="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605816027p2/2905339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1378950554?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1378950554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14278808021807921613"><a href='http://s61.photobucket.com/user/barklesswagmore/media/hoarder_zpsnsubrrkz.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471359279i/20036119.jpg' alt=' photo hoarder_zpsnsubrrkz.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I know a secret. If you have too much stuff and it‚Äôs bugging you then get rid of it. All of it. Well, nearly all of it. Save a few things but only the things you absolutely love, the things that spark joy within your being (you‚Äôll know it when you feel it, says the author) and don‚Äôt bring more things into the house unless you love and/or need them. Don‚Äôt think you can do that? Well, never mind then.<br/><br/>This author wants you to be absolutely ruthless with your possessions and do it in one fell sw</span>
  <span id="freeText14278808021807921613" style="display:none"><a href="http://s61.photobucket.com/user/barklesswagmore/media/hoarder_zpsnsubrrkz.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471359279i/20036119.jpg" alt=" photo hoarder_zpsnsubrrkz.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I know a secret. If you have too much stuff and it‚Äôs bugging you then get rid of it. All of it. Well, nearly all of it. Save a few things but only the things you absolutely love, the things that spark joy within your being (you‚Äôll know it when you feel it, says the author) and don‚Äôt bring more things into the house unless you love and/or need them. Don‚Äôt think you can do that? Well, never mind then.<br><br>This author wants you to be absolutely ruthless with your possessions and do it in one fell swoop. Don‚Äôt dilly-dally and put certain unpleasant things off. Absolutely do not waste money buying ‚Äústorage solutions‚Äù. Just get rid of your stuff and you won‚Äôt have to store it or dust it or leave it there to feel bad for itself. Now, none of this is a bad thing (though the last might be a wee bit kooky) and honestly I‚Äôm all for it. I had way too much crap lying about and it was driving me crazy. Broken crap, ugly crap, gifted crap, crap that had been there so long it was invisible to me. But this book has a problem and it is a BIG one that I‚Äôm betting many of you here on this site may take issue with as well. <br><br><a href="http://s61.photobucket.com/user/barklesswagmore/media/321_zpsgpdoticv.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471359559i/20036140.jpg" alt=" photo 321_zpsgpdoticv.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Step #2, you see, is books. BOOKS! Step freaking two is BOOKS. As you can probably easily imagine, I am stuck here on step #2 because, well, it‚Äôs a call to action to rid myself of my precious books! I‚Äôve been collecting books since I was twelve years old. I have a lot of books but I‚Äôm afraid I may love them all. <br><br>#1 was clothes, shoes, accessories and that was a breeze. Who needs clothes taking up space that could hold a few books? This was easy, thought I. My closet was done in an hour or so. Everything culled, sorted and color coded and folded all nice and tidy-like. I could blow through this, thought I. A zen and clutter-free life was within my grasp. I had this. Then step #2 happened and I was instructed to rid myself of all of the books I have loved before (but may not love again) and all of the books I have not read yet. Uh oh. I was told to remove my TBR pile(s) from my life. Forever. And almost always. She‚Äôll allow you to re-buy digitally if you are pining away and dying of sadness for it. I was instructed to touch each one and see if it sparked that apparently not-so-elusive feeling of joy within me. Trouble is they all kind of did. I suppose I am broken. I tried folks, I truly did. I took pictures and even posted them online in an attempt to humiliate myself into following through. I even went so far as removing a gigantor bookshelf, stocked three piles deep, floor-to-ceiling, from my room as well as an armoire I no longer needed. I have to admit my room looks and feels calms and free and spacious. The bookshelf now neatly resides in my basement. I pulled off all of the books and starting sorting them but it made me incredibly sad to think about tossing them out of my house where they might potentially end up in a trash/recycle bin (according to the author everything has feelings so how could I allow this? Better they be a little lonesome on my shelf than DEAD, right?!). Instead of tossing them into bags, I started arranging them by color (which she wants you to do with clothes) and then I put all but a dozen or so back up on the shelves. They look happy and pretty and they brighten the back wall of the basement. I have decided that I am keeping them. They are my one and only vice and I work hard. They are not clutter.<br><br>I think I shall pretend that step 2 was nothing but a fever dream.<br><br>After I was revived with sniffing salts I got back to business. So next comes all of the other stuff which I can easily part ways with; the paper, the stuff no one ever eats, the gadgets (my days of bread baking are over), the broken things that we‚Äôve been thinking we‚Äôll fix someday, the mementos, pictures and all the other useless crapola that has been residing in the basement since we moved in a million years ago. I‚Äôve removed countless bags of trash and several car loads of ‚Äústuff‚Äù and hauled them to Goodwill and I miss none of it. It is so much easier to clean my house now. I haven‚Äôt followed this plan as written, it‚Äôs difficult when you live with several other people, so we still have some bins and crud to get to but now I'm inspired to keep at it.<br><br>This book will give you some unique tools and I do recommend it if you skip step two or perhaps save it for last, if you‚Äôre anything like me. She has a nifty way of folding clothes that helped me fit everything into a few drawers and will keep me in check if I decide I need more yoga pants. You really do see just how much of each clothing category you own when you pile them all on the bed/floor and separate them into their own little categories. She doesn‚Äôt declutter by room but by category. This stops you from getting stuck (on pictures or mementos which are left for the end) and forces you to deal with an entire category and actually finish the job so you never have to do it again. She also tells you to start with a clear vision of your end result. That bit of advice has helped me tremendously.<br><br>The author clearly has an obsession with tidying. She does not deny this. Apparently, she‚Äôs been this way since she was a wee, strange child and goes into great detail at the beginning of book about her childhood hobby of ‚Äútidying‚Äù. This makes the start a bit of a slog. I found some of her beliefs a little quirky and I will not be emptying my bag out each night so my stuff can ‚Äúbreathe‚Äù only to put everything back in come morning (what the?!) but if you can overlook some of the odd things she says, you‚Äôll more than likely find something here to help you out.<br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14278808021807921613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1122960693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15369159429253968558">Notes as i read:<br/><br/>Things I like:<br/>-the idea of tidying by category<br/>-the joy factor <br/>-"we should be choosing what we want to keep, not what we want to get rid of."<br/>-she's not very judgemental <br/>-the sweet Japanese anthropomorphizing of objects<br/>-her approach to clothes and thanking the objects for their service <br/>-her order and suggestion that tidying needs to be done just once in a big swoop and in a certain order: discard first, figure out where things go after<br/>-like the idea of seeing what you need/don't ne</span>
  <span id="freeText15369159429253968558" style="display:none">Notes as i read:<br /><br />Things I like:<br />-the idea of tidying by category<br />-the joy factor <br />-"we should be choosing what we want to keep, not what we want to get rid of."<br />-she's not very judgemental <br />-the sweet Japanese anthropomorphizing of objects<br />-her approach to clothes and thanking the objects for their service <br />-her order and suggestion that tidying needs to be done just once in a big swoop and in a certain order: discard first, figure out where things go after<br />-like the idea of seeing what you need/don't need as an act of vulnerability and strength growing <br /><br />Things that don't jive:<br /><br />-She has no concept of the archive<br />-one problem i have with the method is that there are things i have to own that don't bring me joy...i can't get rid of my interview clothes. do they bring me joy? no. Do i need them for when i am seeking a new job? yes.<br />- The book is also very gendered, i feel. Not in a totally offensive way, but in a noticeable way. <br />-hahahaha like I'm going to get rid of books hahahaha (skimmed this section)<br />-hahahaha like I'm going to get rid of paper hahahaha (skimmed this section)<br />-she's not an artist. I can't really apply her theory to my art supplies. I mean, i can to a point, but hello...i have millions of pieces of metal type. The studio is off limits to her. sorry. <br />-class. This assumes you have the money to replace what is broken but still usable or not hold onto outgrown kids clothes that could be used for the next kid.<br />-finding the last section of the book tedious and a bit eye roll-y<br /><br />The book was probably written when the author was 25...or younger. I'm not going to take her method to gospel but i do think that I will give it a go, esp. in terms of clothing. It's mostly charming, though there are things I'm just not willing to let go of and that's ok too. It's my choice</span>

<div id="review_1243736366" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1243736366" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1243736366?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kats" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kats" href="/user/show/4786937-kats">Kats</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243736366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12029501383963713162">What will I take away from this "life changing" book on tidying up? <br/><br/>1. If you name a method after yourself, you conjure up instant credibility as an "expert". <br/>2. If you are a neurotic nutcase with an obsessive-compulsive disorder, try to turn it into a virtue, or even better, a lucrative career.<br/>3. If you use the words "spark joy", "feel happiness" and "reduce anxiety" enough times, people will want to follow your lead and pay you good money for your advice. <br/><br/>and on a practical level I've learnt t</span>
  <span id="freeText12029501383963713162" style="display:none">What will I take away from this "life changing" book on tidying up? <br /><br />1. If you name a method after yourself, you conjure up instant credibility as an "expert". <br />2. If you are a neurotic nutcase with an obsessive-compulsive disorder, try to turn it into a virtue, or even better, a lucrative career.<br />3. If you use the words "spark joy", "feel happiness" and "reduce anxiety" enough times, people will want to follow your lead and pay you good money for your advice. <br /><br />and on a practical level I've learnt that <br /><br />1. you can apply origami skills to any item of clothing (it may take years to master the art of folding your stockings, but apparently it will save you lots of time in the long run) <br />2. you ought to store everything vertically, whether that's knickers, pencils or a waffle iron (but only if that waffle iron *sparks joy* in you, obviously). <br />3. the ideal situation is to live in a bare, sterile home, and should anyone dare to give you an ornament or any other tangible gift, discard it at the earliest opportunity by saying "thank you, object X, for teaching me that I'm better off without you". <br />4. "reading clouds your judgment". <br /><br />and for future reference: <br /><br />You thought there was no space in Switzerland? Well, don't ever think about moving to Japan, unless you are ready to throw out everything you have, and that probably includes your children. <br /><br />Yeah, you guessed it, this Marie Kondo won't be coming to my house in her frilly dresses any time soon to have that dialogue with my house, clothes and handbags about how hard they work for me. No thanks. I rather continue to live happily with all my clutter and mess. <br /><br />---------------------------------------------------- <br /><br />After posting my review I checked out what other people had to say about the KonMari craze, and the first review I read is so brilliant and hit the nail on the head, so here is the link: <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1171393193?book_show_action=true&amp;page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/971061-edh?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1135221857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9878872391193390091">I've read a lot of organization books over the years, but this is a book that might actually change your relationship with your possessions. Instead of focusing on categories, fiddly buckets, or accessories from Bed Bath and Beyond, Marie Kondo asks us to reevaluate the way we relate to our homes and belongings. The question, "does this spark joy?" seems pat, but it truly liberates you to think critically why you keep something around. By the end of the book, you'll understand that we keep thing</span>
  <span id="freeText9878872391193390091" style="display:none">I've read a lot of organization books over the years, but this is a book that might actually change your relationship with your possessions. Instead of focusing on categories, fiddly buckets, or accessories from Bed Bath and Beyond, Marie Kondo asks us to reevaluate the way we relate to our homes and belongings. The question, "does this spark joy?" seems pat, but it truly liberates you to think critically why you keep something around. By the end of the book, you'll understand that we keep things that don't enhance our current lives because we are not fully living in the present - that we cannot let go of the past, or are not yet ready to make room for something new in our future. A transformative look at consumerism and its discontents in the 21st century, with extremely helpful tips to help you make deliberate decisions about what to keep, and what to thank and let go of. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9878872391193390091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2298341956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2298341956" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2298341956?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2298341956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3605645738276377128">I picked up this book because so many people talk about it, but I'm not necessarily a hoarder or someone who has too many things that I need to tidy up. This was only four hours long on audiobook so I flew through it in two sittings (while cleaning my room, coincidentally). And although I don't agree with Marie a ton about thinning down on your things (ie. for sentimental items, she's like "throw them away!! it had value to you once and now it's gone!!" like, no. im keeping everything i've touch</span>
  <span id="freeText3605645738276377128" style="display:none">I picked up this book because so many people talk about it, but I'm not necessarily a hoarder or someone who has too many things that I need to tidy up. This was only four hours long on audiobook so I flew through it in two sittings (while cleaning my room, coincidentally). And although I don't agree with Marie a ton about thinning down on your things (ie. for sentimental items, she's like "throw them away!! it had value to you once and now it's gone!!" like, no. im keeping everything i've touched until i die lol), I do think a lot of her advice is helpful. Some testimonies about weight loss and having people's life turn around after tidying seemed a liiiittle far fetched, but still, if this method helped some people get in a good headspace, I'm not discounting that.<br /><br />The thing I didn't expect from this book and I think is really valuable is the discussion about appreciating your things. This isn't a book about tidying so much as a book about only keeping the things that matter to you. America is such a materialistic society and this book is a good reminder to be nice to the things you own and to find value in everything, otherwise it isn't worth keeping. I don't think i'll be saying to my clothes, "thank you for keeping me warm" like Marie does, but it was a nice nudge to recognize that owning a lot of things is a privilege, and you can pass on any stuff that has already fulfilled its purpose in your life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3605645738276377128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1124846748" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10141476710711463827">The Office Kat brought this book to my attention, and it became my plane read for a trip to Australia in November 2014. Doubtless the Kat had an ulterior motive (the office is a stacked up mess) but this book offers more than tips on tidying.<br/><br/>The author, Marie Kondo, has made tidying up her life since she was a small child, and shares many anecdotes about her early days as a stealth clutter-control operative in her family home, as well as some of the false starts she had on her way to her tidying</span>
  <span id="freeText10141476710711463827" style="display:none">The Office Kat brought this book to my attention, and it became my plane read for a trip to Australia in November 2014. Doubtless the Kat had an ulterior motive (the office is a stacked up mess) but this book offers more than tips on tidying.<br /><br />The author, Marie Kondo, has made tidying up her life since she was a small child, and shares many anecdotes about her early days as a stealth clutter-control operative in her family home, as well as some of the false starts she had on her way to her tidying method. <br /><br />I will not steal her thunder by revealing her unorthodox methods, but will say it has already worked a magic on one kitchen that I used to dread entering. If one has the will, the method works, and she is also right that I have no desire to go back to my old ways in that kitchen. <br /><br />I think I will apply this method to my clothing and office.<br /><br />Books and papers? well, I may need to build up to that!</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=self-help">self-help</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2420830482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16099805681890720244">Marie Kond≈ç‚Äôs approach to de-cluttering is worth considering, but also challenging, seeing that it involves human beings treating objects with kindness and respect. That is perhaps only possible for people who have achieved or strive to achieve self-actualization. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3582487555" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3582487555" />
    <a title="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2744708-jess-the-shelf-declared-bibliophile"><img alt="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606058182p2/2744708.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3582487555?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" href="/user/show/2744708-jess-the-shelf-declared-bibliophile">Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3582487555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15104949905332549734">When I first started this book, it felt absolutely life changing. I was already facing a looming "fall cleaning", as I had family coming to visit and I usually do a deep house cleaning before the holiday decorating starts anyway. <br/><br/>After a couple of chapters, I immediately spent a couple of days going through just about everything in the house and loaded up around 5 trashbags to be donated, as well as 2 large boxfuls of books, and that's not even counting all I threw away (which was also a lot!). </span>
  <span id="freeText15104949905332549734" style="display:none">When I first started this book, it felt absolutely life changing. I was already facing a looming "fall cleaning", as I had family coming to visit and I usually do a deep house cleaning before the holiday decorating starts anyway. <br /><br />After a couple of chapters, I immediately spent a couple of days going through just about everything in the house and loaded up around 5 trashbags to be donated, as well as 2 large boxfuls of books, and that's not even counting all I threw away (which was also a lot!). I inadvertently even influenced my girlfriend to fill a couple of trashbags with clothes to be donated, and that's saying much for someone who HATES going through clothes. <br /><br />I feel this book definitely helped my aspect on how to treat my possessions and home, and gave me a plethora of ways I can work on improving both. I don't buy in to ALL of her methods, like throwing every piece of clothing in the middle of a room and feeling them one by one to see which sparks joy. That would take me a month! Same with all my books! However, I definitely have taken a lot from this, and I would recommend it to anyone. It lost some stars as I trucked through to the end as it started to feel a bit repetitive and even silly at times, like speaking to my possessions and home and giving thanks to them every day. I definitely believe in positive energy but not necessarily actually communicating with inanimate objects. Overall, worth the read, but some of it perhaps take with a grain of salt. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15104949905332549734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nGll/Y2QMruSc0L++8eVphMhvn/vyrn7HYi4B6DE/hQrdcHr/jXwxdCZ0JG1HRwPFINBFsp/w9Qd3qBtHRZHjQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vVP2LHJSKErjx5k451DNy+1D7Do6JdfKHcvxsCzzczQKT1I6AffqNKEtC1epikRi6uETUx+QreUdnenakSHKrQ==')})
  }

The illustrations also show Ms Kondo\'s unique folding method, clearly showing how to fold anything from shirts, trousers and jackets to skirts, socks and bras.\n\nThe secret to Marie Kondo\'s unique and simple KonMari tidying method is to focus on what you want to keep, not what you want to get rid of. Ask yourself if something \'sparks joy\' and suddenly it becomes so much easier to understand if you really need it in your home and your life. When you surround yourself with things you love you will find that your whole life begins to change.\n\nMarie Kondo\'s first book, The Life-Changing Magic of Tidying, presents her unique tidying philosophy and introduces readers to the basics of her KonMari method. It has already transformed the homes and lives of millions of people around the world.
